- Has BeginUpdate()/EndUpdate() using WM_SETREDRAW P/Invoke:
```csharp
[DllImport("user32.dll")]
private static extern int SendMessage(IntPtr hWnd, int msg, bool wParam, int lParam);
private const int WM_SETREDRAW = 11;

public void BeginUpdate()
{
    if (IsHandleCreated)
        SendMessage(Handle, WM_SETREDRAW, false, 0);
}

public void EndUpdate()
{
    if (IsHandleCreated)
    {
        SendMessage(Handle, WM_SETREDRAW, true, 0);
        Invalidate(true);
    }
}
```
- This is called every 50ms from Form1.UpdateDisplay when Form2 is visible
- Causes visible flashing/strobing of tabs because WM_SETREDRAW(false) on whole form then Invalidate(true) at 20Hz

4. Errors and Fixes:
- **TelemetryDecoder.cs truncated by sed command**: sed replaced comment text but truncated the end of the file at `d.` in DecodeLowRate_Frame8. Edit tool failed to match due to no newline at EOF. Fixed with Python script that found and replaced the truncated fragment, restoring the missing decode lines + U() helper + closing braces.
- **Compile error CS1001/CS1002/CS1513 at line 662**: Caused by the truncated `d.` fragment. Fixed by the Python repair above.
- **sgsim timing (62.5% speed)**: Caused by (a) RealTime=0 so no pacing, and (b) Sleep(5) overshoots with 15.6ms Windows timer. Fixed with timeBeginPeriod(1) + Sleep(1). User also needs to set "Real time"="Yes" in sgsim Properties.

5. Problem Solving:
- **sgsim packet layout vs ICD**: The running sgsim binary (HSL_31_JAN_2017) uses different section boundaries than the ICD. Full Rate is 68B (not 58B), so HR starts at pkt[72] not pkt[62]. The 288° heading observation was explained by MSVC debug build filling unwritten FullRateBuff[58..59] with 0xCC → Heading = 0xCCCC/65535*360 = 288°. All HR and LR fields were being decoded from wrong bytes.
- **GCS display lag**: Four sources identified and three fixed (Console.WriteLine, 100ms timer, synchronous Refresh). Fourth (per-setter Invalidate in AxCombined) is minor.
- **Form2 tab flashing** (current): WM_SETREDRAW on the entire form at 20Hz causes visible strobe. Need to fix without losing the benefit of batched label updates.

8. Current Work:
Immediately before this summary request, the user reported: "On scrn2, the tabs are flashing; they need to be constant." This refers to Form2.cs (the secondary display). The flashing is caused by `BeginUpdate()`/`EndUpdate()` which applies `WM_SETREDRAW(false)` then `WM_SETREDRAW(true)` + `Invalidate(true)` on the entire Form2 window at 20Hz. The sudden redraw enable + full invalidate at every display tick creates a visible strobe effect on the TabControl tabs.

9. Optional Next Step:
Fix Form2 tab flashing. The user said: "On scrn2, the tabs are flashing; they need to be constant."

The fix is to change Form2's `BeginUpdate()`/`EndUpdate()` so it applies `WM_SETREDRAW` to the **TabControl** (or just the active TabPage) rather than the entire Form2 window. This way the tabs themselves (the tab strip header bar) are not affected by the redraw suppression — only the content area is frozen during the label batch update. Alternatively, switch to double-buffering on Form2 and remove WM_SETREDRAW entirely, letting the OS composite all label changes in one frame. A simpler approach: apply WM_SETREDRAW only to `_tabs.SelectedTab` (the currently visible page) rather than `this.Handle`, so the tab header strip never gets frozen.

If you need specific details from before compaction (like exact code snippets, error messages, or content you generated), read the full transcript at: C:\Users\uzama\AppData\Roaming\Claude\local-agent-mode-sessions\c5d91914-32e1-4e8e-8812-0c3a4236b9d0\f8d7fd94-4896-4018-b3e8-2b592b86c6c5\local_350f7462-3a32-430f-959e-4a32f57edc37\.claude\projects\C--Users-uzama-AppData-Roaming-Claude-local-agent-mode-sessions-c5d91914-32e1-4e8e-8812-0c3a4236b9d0-f8d7fd94-4896-4018-b3e8-2b592b86c6c5-local-350f7462-3a32-430f-959e-4a32f57edc37-outputs\d25b5ed0-94f9-40a4-9ff7-e072a67d053e.jsonl

[706] CLAUDE
----------------------------------------
Everything looks correct. The change is complete. To summarize what changed and why:

**Root cause:** `WM_SETREDRAW(false)` was sent to `this.Handle` — Form2's top-level window. The `TabControl` (including the tab header strip) is a child of that window, so the entire form including the tab bar was frozen and then slammed with a full repaint at 20Hz → visible strobe.

**Fix:** `_tc` is now a field. `BeginUpdate`/`EndUpdate` target `_tc.SelectedTab.Handle` — the `TabPage`'s window — which is only the content area inside the currently visible tab. The `TabControl`'s header strip is part of the `TabControl`'s own window (a different HWND), so it is never frozen and never redraws from scratch. The tabs will be stable.

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:

**A. Fix Form2 tab flashing** (completed): "On scrn2, the tabs are flashing; they need to be constant." The tabs strobed at 20Hz because `BeginUpdate()`/`EndUpdate()` applied `WM_SETREDRAW` to `this.Handle` (entire Form2 window), freezing/restoring the TabControl header strip each cycle.

**B. Integrate a real map** (completed): Replace the custom GDI+ coordinate map with real tile imagery. User selected OpenStreetMap tiles, offline operation required ("aircraft operated with no internet"). After GMap.NET.Core proved too difficult to use (opaque API, missing WindowsForms assembly), switched to a fully standalone implementation with direct OSM tile downloads and a file-based cache. User confirmed: "map is working."

**C. Add satellite/standard view toggle** (completed with one compile error fixed): Add radio buttons to switch between OpenStreetMap standard tiles and Esri World Imagery satellite tiles.

**D. Satellite only + waypoint markers on map** (CURRENT — in progress): "use only satellite view. In telemetry data your are receiving way point data, can you mark wpoints on the map."

2. Key Technical Concepts:
- WinForms .NET Framework 4.8, programmatic layout, no Designer
- `WM_SETREDRAW` P/Invoke targeting `TabPage.Handle` vs `Form.Handle` — the tab header strip is part of the `TabControl` HWND, not the `TabPage` HWND, so targeting only the selected `TabPage` prevents tab header flashing
- OSM slippy-map tile math: `LonToTileX = (lon+180)/360 * 2^z`, `LatToTileY = (1 - ln(tan(r)+sec(r))/π) / 2 * 2^z`
- Esri World Imagery tile URL format: `https://server.arcgisonline.com/ArcGIS/rest/services/World_Imagery/MapServer/tile/{z}/{y}/{x}` — note **y/x swapped** vs OSM `{z}/{x}/{y}`
- File-based tile cache: `%LocalAppData%\GCS_240626\tiles\{layer}\{z}\{x}\{y}.png`
- Async tile loading: `SemaphoreSlim(4,4)` + `Task.Run` + `BeginInvoke(Invalidate)`
- `System.Net.WebClient.DownloadDataTaskAsync` for tile downloads
- `MapLayer` enum (`Standard`, `Satellite`) with separate cache subfolders (`osm/`, `sat/`)
- TileKey struct includes layer field `L` to prevent cross-layer cache collisions

public void BeginUpdate()
{
    var page = _tc?.SelectedTab;
    if (page != null && page.IsHandleCreated)
        SendMessage(page.Handle, WM_SETREDRAW, false, 0);
}
public void EndUpdate()
{
    var page = _tc?.SelectedTab;
    if (page != null && page.IsHandleCreated)
    {
        SendMessage(page.Handle, WM_SETREDRAW, true, 0);
        page.Invalidate(true);
    }
}
```

    => layer == MapLayer.Standard
       ? $"https://tile.openstreetmap.org/{z}/{x}/{y}.png"
       : $"https://server.arcgisonline.com/ArcGIS/rest/services/World_Imagery/MapServer/tile/{z}/{y}/{x}";

private static string LayerFolder(MapLayer layer)
    => layer == MapLayer.Standard ? "osm" : "sat";

private static string TilePath(TileKey k)
    => Path.Combine(CacheRoot, LayerFolder(k.L),
                    k.Z.ToString(), k.X.ToString(), k.Y + ".png");
```

[809] CLAUDE
----------------------------------------
Here's the complete picture of the mission download protocol:

**Data destination:** Received packets decode into `MissionData.MP_WPData[]`. After `ACTIVATE_MISSION` + CRC check passes, they copy across to `MissionData.WPData[]` (the live mission).

**Transport:** Same serial channel as telemetry. Every packet is exactly **32 bytes binary**:
```
[0]     Vehicle ID
[1]     Command
[2-3]   WP Number (uint16 LE)
[4-27]  Data payload (24 bytes)
[28-31] CRC-32 of bytes 0–27
```

**Upload sequence:** `HEADER_WRITE (0x51)` → `WP_WRITE (0x01)` × N → `POI_WRITE (0xB0)` if POIFlag → `SEARCH_WRITE (0xC0)` if SearchFlag → `ACTIVATE_MISSION (0xA1)`. FCC sends an ACK after each packet.

**WP encoding (bytes 4–27):**
```
[4-7]   Lat      = (lat + 90.0)   × 23 860 929.4167   → uint32 LE
[8-11]  Lon      = (lon + 180.0)  × 11 930 464.7083   → uint32 LE
[12-14] Alt      = alt            × 838.8608           → uint24 LE
[15-16] CSpeed   = cspeed         × 655.35             → uint16 LE
[17-18] LtrAlt   = ltralt         × 3.27675            → uint16 LE
[19]    LtrRadius= ltrradius      × 0.0510             → byte
[20-21] LtrSpeed = ltrspeed       × 655.35             → uint16 LE
[22]    LtrTime                                         → byte (min)
[23-26] 0x00
[27]    Flags: bit0=LtrFlag  bit1=POIFlag  bit2=SearchFlag
```

---

So the output the GCS needs to produce for serial TX is **not text — it's a binary packet stream**: one 32-byte packet per command, in sequence. The `.mpr` text file was the mission planning tool's storage format; what actually goes over the wire is these fixed binary packets.

Should I implement a `MissionPacketEncoder` class in the GCS that takes a loaded `MissionData` and produces the binary packet stream (ready to be sent byte-by-byte over serial)? That can be written to a `.bin` file now and wired to the serial port later.

[810] USER
----------------------------------------
Should I implement a `MissionPacketEncoder` class in the GCS

[811] CLAUDE
----------------------------------------
Yes, go ahead.

----------------------------------------
yes

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- WinForms .NET Framework 4.8, programmatic layout, no Designer
- Esri World Imagery satellite tiles: `https://server.arcgisonline.com/ArcGIS/rest/services/World_Imagery/MapServer/tile/{z}/{y}/{x}` (y and x swapped vs OSM)
- File-based tile cache: `%LocalAppData%\GCS_240626\tiles\sat\{z}\{y}\{x}.jpg`
- UAV icon PNG: 80×80 RGBA, nose pointing up (−Y), loaded from `Application.ExecutablePath` directory
- Binary `.mfp` mission format: 128-byte header + 24-byte GCS + 112-byte takeoff + 104-byte landing + WPCount×152-byte WPs + 4-byte CRC-32
- Per-WP record: 8 flag bytes + 17 doubles (136 bytes) + 8 reserved = 152 bytes
- CRC-32 standard polynomial 0xEDB88320
- sgsim mission programming: 32-byte binary packets over telemetry serial channel
- Fixed-point encoding for Lat/Lon/Alt/speeds in mission packets
- `MissionData.MP_WPData[]` = received buffer; copied to `MissionData.WPData[]` after ACTIVATE_MISSION

**`C:\Users\uzama\source\repos\GCS_240626\MissionFile.cs`** — NEW FILE. Key types and methods:
```csharp
public enum WPCategory : byte { Waypoint=0, BStation=1, LandApproach=2, TakeoffTaxi=3 }

public struct LLAPoint { public double Lat, Lon, Alt; }

public class MissionWP {
    public bool DataValid; public WPCategory Category; public ushort Number;
    public bool LtrFlag, SearchFlag, POIFlag, RadioSilenceFlag;
    public double Lat, Lon, Alt, CSpeed;
    public double LtrTime, LtrRadius, LtrSpeed, LtrAlt;
    public double SearchBearing, SearchWidth, SearchLength, SearchTime, SearchSpeed, SearchAlt;
    public double POILat, POILon, POIAlt;
}

public class MissionData {
    public string Name, CreatedBy; public DateTime CreateDate; public int UAV_ID;
    public LLAPoint GCS;
    public LLAPoint TORunwayEnd1, TORunwayEnd2, ClimbOutEnd1, ClimbOutEnd2;
    public double TORunwayWidth, AbortTaxiDist;
    public LLAPoint LandRunwayEnd1, LandRunwayEnd2, LAPoint1, LAPoint2;
    public double LandRunwayWidth;
    public readonly List<MissionWP> WayPoints = new List<MissionWP>();
}

public static class MissionFile {
    public static MissionData Read(string path);       // auto-detect .mfp or .mpr
    public static MissionData ReadMfp(string path);    // binary format
    public static void WriteMfp(string path, MissionData md);  // binary + CRC32 at end
    public static MissionData ReadMpr(string path);    // legacy text INI
    public static void WriteMpr(string path, MissionData md);  // text for serial TX
    public static uint Crc32(byte[] data, int offset, int count);
}
```

Binary `.mfp` layout (offsets):
- 0: magic "MSSN", version, UAV_ID, WPCount, flags
- 8: MissionName[64], CreatedBy[16], timestamp(uint32), reserved[36] → total 128
- 128: GCS Lat/Lon/Alt (3 doubles = 24 bytes)
- 152: TOEnd1, TOEnd2, ClimbOutEnd1, ClimbOutEnd2 (4×24), TORunwayWidth, AbortTaxiDist (2×8) = 112 bytes
- 264: LandEnd1, LandEnd2, LAPoint1, LAPoint2 (4×24), LandRunwayWidth (8) = 104 bytes
- 368: WP records (WPCount × 152 bytes)
- End-4: CRC-32 (4 bytes)

Per-WP record (152 bytes):
```
[0]   DataValid (byte)
[1]   Category (byte)
[2-3] WPNumber (uint16 LE)
[4]   LtrFlag, [5] SearchFlag, [6] POIFlag, [7] RadioSilenceFlag
[8..] 17 doubles: Lat,Lon,Alt,CSpeed,LtrTime,LtrRadius,LtrSpeed,LtrAlt,
      SearchBearing,SearchWidth,SearchLength,SearchTime,SearchSpeed,SearchAlt,
      POILat,POILon,POIAlt
[+8 reserved bytes]
```

**`D:\DOCUMENT\NFCC Local\Airframe\AP_SW\HILS Related\SW hil\HSL_31_JAN_2017\sgsim\simcode\autop\MissionProgramming.c`** — Read-only investigation. Key findings:

Complete 32-byte binary packet protocol:
```
[0]     Vehicle ID
[1]     Command byte
[2-3]   WP Number (uint16 LE)
[4-27]  Data payload (24 bytes)
[28-31] CRC-32 of bytes 0-27
```

Command bytes:
```
HEADER_WRITE=0x51, HEADER_READ=0x52, HEADER_DELETE=0x53
WP_WRITE=0x01, WP_READ=0x02, WP_DELETE=0x03
POI_WRITE=0xB0, POI_READ=0xB1, POI_DELETE=0xB2
SEARCH_WRITE=0xC0, SEARCH_READ=0xC1, SEARCH_DELETE=0xC2
CRC_READ=0xA0, ACTIVATE_MISSION=0xA1, FILE_DELETE=0xA2
```

WP_WRITE encoding (bytes 4-27):
```
[4-7]   Lat:      uint32 = (lat + 90.0) × 23860929.416666700
[8-11]  Lon:      uint32 = (lon + 180.0) × 11930464.70833330
[12-14] Alt:      uint24 = alt × 838.860750
[15-16] CSpeed:   uint16 = cspeed × 655.350
[17-18] LtrAlt:   uint16 = ltralt × 3.276750
[19]    LtrRadius: byte  = ltrradius × 0.0510
[20-21] LtrSpeed: uint16 = ltrspeed × 655.350
[22]    LtrTime:  byte (minutes)
[23-26] zeros
[27]    flags: bit0=LtrFlag, bit1=POIFlag, bit2=SearchFlag
```

POI_WRITE encoding (bytes 4-14):
```
[4-7]  POILat: uint32 = (poilat + 90) × 23860929.41666670
[8-11] POILon: uint32 = (poilon + 180) × 11930464.70833330
[12-14] POIAlt: uint24 = poialt × 838.860750
[15-27] zeros
```

SEARCH_WRITE encoding (bytes 4-14):
```
[4-5]  SearchBearing: uint16 = bearing × 182.04166666670
[6-7]  SearchWidth:   uint16 = width × 13.1070
[8-9]  SearchLength:  uint16 = length × 3.276750
[10]   SearchTime:    byte (min)
[11-12] SearchSpeed:  uint16 = speed × 655.350
[13-14] SearchAlt:    uint16 = alt × 3.276750
[15-27] zeros
```

HEADER_WRITE encoding (bytes 4-27):
```
[4-11]  TimeStamp (8 bytes, long double)
[12]    UAV ID
[13-21] Name (9 bytes ASCII)
[22-23] TotalWP (uint16 LE)
[24-27] File CRC (reserved/commented out in code)
```

Upload sequence: HEADER_WRITE → WP_WRITE×N → POI_WRITE (if POIFlag) → SEARCH_WRITE (if SearchFlag) → ACTIVATE_MISSION

ACK codes: OK=0x01, HEADER_INVALID=0x02, WP_INVALID=0x03, WP_LIM_EXCEDED=0x04, ALL_WP_NOT_RECEIVED=0x05, FILE_NOT_EXIST=0x06, HEADER_NOT_RECEIVED=0x07, POI_NOT_EXIST=0x08, SEARCH_NOT_EXIST=0x09, MISSION_CRC_FAILED=0x10, MISSION_PROG_DENIED=0x11

4. Errors and Fixes:

- **Python WP record size assertion (160 ≠ 152)**: Python script wrote 18 doubles (`'<18d'` including a padding double) instead of 17 doubles + 8 reserved bytes. Fixed by using `struct.pack('<17d', *vals)` then `bytes(8)` separately, giving 8+136+8=152 bytes ✓

- **.mpr CRC mismatch**: The CRC value in the .mpr header (`2796251641`) does not match standard CRC-32 of any obvious file subset — the mission planning tool uses a proprietary CRC algorithm. For the new `.mfp` format, standard CRC-32 (poly 0xEDB88320) is used instead. For `.mpr` output in `WriteMpr()`, CRC-32 of the WP content block is computed and stored in the header.

5. Problem Solving:

- **Mission display vs. TX**: Initially built map display for waypoints; user then said "do not implement on the application map." Removed DrawMission from OnPaint, redirected button to generate text file for serial TX.
- **Icon panning**: Root cause was that DrawAircraft used hardcoded (cx,cy) screen center instead of computing geographic→screen transform. Fixed with ToScreen().
- **Binary protocol discovery**: By reading MissionProgramming.c, the exact 32-byte binary packet protocol was reverse-engineered, providing all scale factors needed for encoding.

`MissionPacketEncoder.cs` is added to the project. Here's what it does and how it fits together:

**On each "📂 Mission" button click**, MapControl now exports two files side-by-side:

| File | Content |
|---|---|
| `<name>.mpr` | Plain-text INI (legacy, documentation) |
| `<name>.bin` | Binary 32-byte packet stream, ready for serial TX |

**Packet sequence in the `.bin` file:**
1. `HEADER_WRITE (0x51)` — mission name, UAV ID, timestamp, WP count
2. `WP_WRITE (0x01)` × N — one per BStation/Waypoint entry, indexed 0..N-1
3. `POI_WRITE (0xB0)` — only emitted if `wp.POIFlag = true`
4. `SEARCH_WRITE (0xC0)` — only emitted if `wp.SearchFlag = true`
5. `ACTIVATE_MISSION (0xA1)` — triggers the FCC CRC check and arm

Each packet is 32 bytes: `[0]=VehicleID [1]=CMD [2-3]=WPNum [4-27]=Data [28-31]=CRC32`.

When you wire this to the serial port later, send the `.bin` file byte-by-byte, waiting for a `0x01` ACK after each 32-byte packet before sending the next.

how this .bin file will be transported to the 'sgsim' app

[821] CLAUDE

The `.bin` file is offline storage only — it still needs an active serial TX channel. Here's the full picture:

**The serial port is already half-wired.** `PacketReceiver` opens `COM9` at 115200 and already has `WriteBufferSize` and `WriteTimeout` set — it's ready to TX, but nothing calls `_port.Write()` yet.

**For sgsim (same machine):** use a virtual COM port pair. com0com is the standard free tool — it creates a loopback pair (e.g. COM9 ↔ COM10). GCS opens COM9 (already does), sgsim opens COM10, and they talk as if wired together.

```
GCS (COM9) ←TX/RX→ [virtual null-modem] ←TX/RX→ sgsim (COM10)
```

**What still needs to be built** is a `MissionUploader` that reads the `.bin` and drives the send-ACK loop:

```
for each 32-byte packet in .bin:
    _port.Write(packet, 0, 32)       ← TX
    wait for 32-byte reply on RX     ← ACK
    check reply[4] == 0x01 (ACK_OK)
    on failure → abort or retry
```

The reason I saved the `.bin` first (rather than streaming directly) is that `PacketReceiver` currently owns the serial port privately — exposing a `Write()` method and adding the ACK-wait logic requires touching that class. That's the next step when you're ready to wire it.

**Order of operations to complete serial TX:**
1. Add `public void Send(byte[] packet)` to `PacketReceiver` — single 32-byte write
2. Add an ACK callback/event to `PacketReceiver` so the uploader can await each response
3. Build `MissionUploader.cs` — reads the `.bin`, sends packet-by-packet with ACK gating
4. Wire a "⬆ Send Mission" button in the GCS to trigger the uploader

Want me to implement steps 1–3 now?

Correct — it's one bidirectional serial link. Same COM9, same baud rate (115200). The FCC uses it for both telemetry out and mission-program ACKs in.

The implication for implementation:

**RX side** already works. `PacketReceiver.DataReceived` is reading the stream continuously. The problem is that during mission upload, 32-byte ACK packets will arrive mixed into the stream alongside normal 164-byte telemetry packets. The existing framing logic needs to handle both sizes.

**TX side** just needs `_port.Write()` exposed — the port is already open.

The cleanest approach: add a TX method to `PacketReceiver` and add an ACK detection path to the existing `DataReceived` handler. The two packet types are distinguishable by byte [1] (command echo) — telemetry packets have their own sync/command structure, ACKs have `byte[1]` matching the command you just sent.

That changes the architecture significantly. There are **two separate serial channels**:

| Channel | Direction | sgsim port | GCS port |
|---|---|---|---|
| Telemetry | FCC → GCS | COM9 (sends) | COM9 (receives) — already done |

Done. Here's the complete picture of what was built:

**PacketReceiver.cs** — 3 additions:
- `SendRaw(byte[])` — writes directly to `_port`
- `BeginMissionUpload()` / `EndMissionUpload()` — mode flag
- `WaitForAck(ms)` — blocks the uploader thread until 32-byte reply arrives (or timeout)

**MissionUploader.cs** — async loop: encode → send each packet → wait ACK → retry up to 3× on timeout/NACK → report progress → return bool success

**MapControl.cs** — `⬆ Send` button (enabled after mission loads) fires `MissionSendRequested` event; `ReportUploadStatus()` lets Form1 push TX progress back into the map status bar

**Form1.cs** — subscribes to `MissionSendRequested`, runs `MissionUploader.UploadAsync` on a background task, progress marshalled back to UI thread automatically via `Progress<T>`

The TX flow end-to-end: click `⬆ Send` → Form1 → `MissionUploader` (background thread) → `PacketReceiver.SendRaw` → COM9 → COM24 → sgsim.

Here's the complete GCS mission upload chain:

---

**1. `MissionFile.cs`** — Data model + file I/O
- Defines `MissionData`, `MissionWP`, `WPCategory` (Waypoint, BStation, LandApproach, TakeoffTaxi)

**2. `MissionPacketEncoder.cs`** — Encodes mission into 32-byte binary packets
- Reverse-engineered from `MissionProgramming.c` in the sgsim source
- Packet layout: `[0]=VehicleID  [1]=CMD  [2-3]=WPNum  [4-27]=Data  [28-31]=CRC32`
- Upload sequence: `HEADER_WRITE → WP_WRITE×N → POI_WRITE (if POIFlag) → SEARCH_WRITE (if SearchFlag) → ACTIVATE_MISSION`
- Only BStation (WP0) + Waypoint category entries are encoded — LP/TK runway markers are map-display only
- All scale factors from the FCC source (e.g. Lat: `(lat+90) × 23860929.42`)
- `WriteToFile()` saves the complete stream as a `.bin` file

---

**3. `MissionUploader.cs`** — Async send-ACK loop
- Takes a `MissionData`, encodes it, sends each 32-byte packet via `PacketReceiver.SendRaw()`
- Waits up to 2000ms for ACK after each packet
- Retries up to 3× on timeout or retryable NACK
- Aborts immediately on fatal NACKs (`WP_LIM_EXCEEDED`, `MISSION_PROG_DENIED`)
- Reports progress via `IProgress<MissionUploadProgress>` (packet count + status string)

---

**4. `PacketReceiver.cs`** — Serial TX + ACK routing added to existing RX
- `SendRaw(byte[])` — writes directly to the open `SerialPort`
- `BeginMissionUpload()` / `EndMissionUpload()` — sets a mode flag
- Modified `ProcessBuffer()`: when upload is active, incoming bytes that don't start with the telemetry sync `0xAA 0x55 0xDD` are treated as 32-byte ACK packets and routed to a `SemaphoreSlim` gate
- `WaitForAck(ms)` — blocks the uploader thread until ACK arrives or timeout
- Telemetry receive continues uninterrupted on the same COM9 port

---

**5. `MapControl.cs` + `Form1.cs`** — UI wiring
- `📂 Mission` button: loads `.mfp`/`.mpr` → saves `.mpr` text + `.bin` packet stream → enables `⬆ Send` button
- `⬆ Send` button: fires `MissionSendRequested` event with loaded `MissionData`
- `Form1` subscribes, runs `MissionUploader.UploadAsync()` on a background thread
- Progress feeds back to the map status bar via `Progress<T>` (marshalled to UI thread automatically)

---

**Serial path:** `GCS COM9 → [virtual pair] → sgsim COM24`

Same COM9 used for telemetry RX and mission TX — bidirectional, framed by packet type (164-byte telemetry vs 32-byte mission ACK).

**What's not yet tested:** the end-to-end ACK response from sgsim — we haven't confirmed that sgsim actually sends a 32-byte reply on COM24 in response to mission packets. That's the next validation step.

When can we download mission data from GCS, assuming sgsim is running

[844] CLAUDE
----------------------------------------
Good question — we've only implemented upload (GCS → FCC). Download is the reverse. Let me read the sgsim source to understand exactly what state the FCC needs to be in and what the response packets look like.

[845] CLAUDE
----------------------------------------
Here's what the sgsim source tells us about download:

**Precondition — a mission must already exist in FCC memory.** The FCC tracks `Header_Written` and `WP_Written` flags. If no mission has been uploaded first, `HEADER_READ` returns `HEADER_INVALID` immediately.

**Download sequence GCS initiates:**

```
GCS sends HEADER_READ (0x52, WP#0)
  → FCC replies with 30-byte header packet  (same layout as HEADER_WRITE data)
  → GCS reads TotalWP from bytes [22-23]

For WP = 0 .. TotalWP-1:
  GCS sends WP_READ (0x02, WP#N)
    → FCC replies with 30-byte WP data  (same encoding as WP_WRITE)
  
  If flags byte [27] bit1 set (POIFlag):
    GCS sends POI_READ (0xB1, WP#N)
      → FCC replies with 30-byte POI data

  If flags byte [27] bit2 set (SearchFlag):
    GCS sends SEARCH_READ (0xC1, WP#N)
      → FCC replies with 30-byte SEARCH data
```

**One important difference from upload:** for READ commands the FCC does **not** call `PrepareAck()`. Instead it fills `MP_Buff[0..29]` and sets `MCData.MP_Tx_Flag = 1`, which triggers the transmit from `SGFltctrl()`. So the GCS receives a **data packet** (not just an ACK byte), and it needs a decoder — the inverse of `MissionPacketEncoder`.

**Summary of when download is possible:**

| Condition | What happens |
|---|---|
| No mission in FCC (`Header_Written = 0`) | HEADER_READ returns `HEADER_INVALID` — cannot download |
| Mission uploaded but not activated | Can download — data is in `MP_WPData[]` buffer |
| Mission activated (`ACTIVATE_MISSION` ACK'd OK) | Can download — same data, now also in `WPData[]` |

So **right now with sgsim running**, you can download as soon as you've done a successful upload first. The GCS side needs a `MissionDownloader` that mirrors the uploader — send READ requests, collect 30-byte data responses, decode them back into `MissionData`. Want me to implement that?

[846] USER
----------------------------------------
What is meant by 'successful upload first' in sgsim? In Sgsim, we select the mission by providing the mission number in 'void PrepareFixedMission(int MissionNo)'

[847] CLAUDE
----------------------------------------
This is an important distinction. Let me show exactly what `PrepareFixedMission` writes to vs. what the READ commands read from:

[848] CLAUDE
----------------------------------------
The answer is clear from the source. There are **two completely separate arrays** in `MissionData`:

| Array | Populated by | Read by |
|---|---|---|
| `WPData[]` | `PrepareFixedMission()` | Autopilot (navigation, guidance) |
| `MP_WPData[]` | `HEADER_WRITE` + `WP_WRITE` from GCS | `ReadAndSendWP()` → `WP_READ` response |

`PrepareFixedMission()` fills `WPData[]` only. It never touches `MP_WPData[]`, never sets `MP_Header.UAVid`, never sets `MP_Header.TotalWP`, and never sets `Header_Written = 1`.

Every READ command in `MissionProgramming.c` guards on:
```c
MissionData.MP_Header.UAVid == VEHICLE_ID &&
WP_Number <= MissionData.MP_Header.TotalWP
```

With a fixed mission, `MP_Header.TotalWP = 0` and `MP_Header.UAVid = 0` — so every `WP_READ` falls through to `WP_INVALID`.

**Bottom line:** The READ/download protocol is not a way to retrieve what `PrepareFixedMission` loaded. It only returns data that was previously written by the GCS via `HEADER_WRITE` + `WP_WRITE`. The two paths are completely independent.

In the real operational workflow:
- **GCS uploads** → `MP_WPData[]` → `ACTIVATE_MISSION` copies to `WPData[]` → autopilot uses it
- **Fixed mission** → `WPData[]` directly, bypassing the whole mission programming channel

So download is useful for **verifying a GCS upload round-trips correctly**, but it cannot retrieve a fixed mission from sgsim. Does that match your understanding of how sgsim is being used?

[868] CLAUDE

The three buttons serve two distinct operations — upload and download are separate directions:

**Upload (GCS → FCC):**
1. **📂 Mission** — opens a file picker, loads the `.mfp`/`.mpr` from disk, also saves a `.bin` packet stream alongside it. Enables the Send button.
2. **⬆ Send** — transmits the loaded mission to the FCC packet-by-packet over COM9, waits for ACKs.

**Download (FCC → GCS):**
3. **↓ DL** — sends READ requests to the FCC, collects the responses, then shows a Save dialog so you can write the received mission as a `.mfp` file. No file selection needed beforehand — the data comes from the FCC.

So the sequence you described — "select a file, then press send" — is the **upload** direction (📂 Mission → ⬆ Send). The **↓ DL** button is self-contained: it goes to the FCC, pulls the mission, and asks you where to save it at the end.

Does this match your intent, or would you prefer a different layout — for example, merging 📂 Mission and ⬆ Send into a single "Upload" button, and renaming ↓ DL to something clearer like "↓ Read FCC"?

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- WinForms .NET Framework 4.8, C# 7.3 (no switch expressions, no C# 8+ features)
- Binary 32-byte mission packet protocol: `[0]=VehicleID [1]=CMD [2-3]=WPNum [4-27]=Data [28-31]=CRC32`
- FCC 36-byte response: `[0-3]=0xAA 0x55 0x55 0xBB` + `[4-31]=28 bytes` + `[32-35]=CRC32`
- Telemetry sync: `0xAA 0x55 0xDD` (164 bytes); Mission response sync: `0xAA 0x55 0x55 0xBB` (36 bytes)
- Two separate mission arrays in sgsim: `WPData[]` (active, used by autopilot) vs `MP_WPData[]` (receive buffer, used by READ/WRITE commands)
- `Header_Written` flag in MissionProgramming.c — only set by HEADER_WRITE from GCS, never by `PrepareFixedMission()`
- Virtual COM port pairing: GCS COM9 ↔ sgsim COM24
- `SemaphoreSlim` ACK gate in PacketReceiver for blocking the upload thread
- `IProgress<MissionUploadProgress>` for cross-thread progress reporting
- `MCData.ActivateNewMission` flag controls whether ACTIVATE_MISSION actually applies the mission
- `GCS_MCData.Enable_Fixed_Mission`: if 1, sgsim ignores GCS mission and uses fixed mission

**`C:\Users\uzama\source\repos\GCS_240626\PacketReceiver.cs`** — critical changes:
```csharp
private const int  MISSION_RESP_LEN  = 36;
private const byte MSYNC0 = 0xAA, MSYNC1 = 0x55, MSYNC2 = 0x55, MSYNC3 = 0xBB;
private volatile bool _missionActive;
private readonly byte[] _lastAck = new byte[MissionPacketEncoder.PACKET_SIZE]; // 32 bytes stripped
private readonly SemaphoreSlim _ackGate = new SemaphoreSlim(0, 1);

public void BeginMissionOp()  => _missionActive = true;
public void EndMissionOp()    => _missionActive = false;
public void BeginMissionUpload() => BeginMissionOp();  // legacy alias
public void EndMissionUpload()   => EndMissionOp();    // legacy alias

public void SendRaw(byte[] data) => _port.Write(data, 0, data.Length);

public byte[] WaitForAck(int timeoutMs = 2000)
{
    if (_ackGate.Wait(timeoutMs))
    {
        lock (_ackLock) { byte[] copy = new byte[32]; Array.Copy(_lastAck, copy, 32); return copy; }
    }
    return null;
}

// In ProcessBuffer():
if (_missionActive &&
    _rxBuf.Count >= MISSION_RESP_LEN &&
    _rxBuf[0] == MSYNC0 && _rxBuf[1] == MSYNC1 &&
    _rxBuf[2] == MSYNC2 && _rxBuf[3] == MSYNC3)
{
    byte[] resp = _rxBuf.GetRange(4, MissionPacketEncoder.PACKET_SIZE).ToArray();
    _rxBuf.RemoveRange(0, MISSION_RESP_LEN);
    lock (_ackLock) Array.Copy(resp, _lastAck, resp.Length);
    try { _ackGate.Release(); } catch (SemaphoreFullException) { }
    continue;
}
```

```c
void Tx_MissProgPacket(unsigned char *Buff) {
    // Copies Buff[0..27] to databuff
    // Appends CRC32 of databuff[0..28) at databuff[28..31]
    // Prepends header: TxBuff[0..3] = 0xAA 0x55 0x55 0xBB
    // TxBuff[4..35] = databuff[0..31]
    // Writes 36 bytes total
}
```

**`D:\DOCUMENT\NFCC Local\Airframe\AP_SW\HILS Related\SW hil\HSL_31_JAN_2017\sgsim\simcode\autop\SGMC.c`** — READ ONLY (key findings):
- `PrepareFixedMission(int MissionNo)` fills `MissionData.WPData[]` directly (NOT MP_WPData[])
- `GCS_MCData.Enable_Fixed_Mission==1` → uses fixed mission, ignores GCS upload
- `MCData.ActivateNewMission=1` only when Mode==STANDBY or RUNUP or (FlightPhase==LOITER && Loiter==GCS_LOITER)
- `MCData.MissionProgrammed=1` after PrepareFixedMission

4. Errors and Fixes:

- **Wrong ACK packet size (32 vs 36 bytes)**: Initial implementation assumed 32-byte ACKs without sync header. `Tx_MissProgPacket()` actually sends 36 bytes with 4-byte sync `0xAA 0x55 0x55 0xBB`. Fixed: `MISSION_RESP_LEN=36`, detect correct sync, strip header before storing in `_lastAck`.

- **Wrong ACK sync detection**: Initial check was `!(_rxBuf[0]==0xAA && _rxBuf[1]==0x55 && _rxBuf[2]==0xDD)` — this would have routed mission responses through the telemetry path since mission sync is `0xAA 0x55 0x55 0xBB` (byte 2 is 0x55 not 0xDD, which would fail the telemetry check but also fail the size check). Fixed: positive match on `0xAA 0x55 0x55 0xBB`.

- **C# 8.0 switch expressions in MissionUploader.cs**: `cmd switch { ... }` and `code switch { ... }` used in `CmdName()` and `AckName()`. Project targets C# 7.3 (.NET Framework 4.8). Fixed: replaced with traditional `switch` statements.

- **Download button hidden by status label**: `_statusLbl` at x=282 with `BringToFront()` covered `_dlMissionBtn` at x=285. Fixed: moved `_statusLbl` to x=470, width=700; moved `_cacheBtn` from x=185 to x=375.

- **Confusing Mission button UX**: Button opened two dialogs — an open dialog then a save dialog for .mpr export. User found this confusing. Fixed: removed both save dialogs, button now only loads into memory and enables ⬆ Send.

5. Problem Solving:

- **Download prerequisite**: `PrepareFixedMission()` in sgsim fills `WPData[]` (active autopilot data) but never sets `Header_Written=1` or fills `MP_WPData[]`. The GCS READ commands require `Header_Written==1` and read from `MP_WPData[]`. Therefore download only works after a GCS upload cycle completes. This is a fundamental architectural constraint of the protocol.

- **Serial link bidirectionality**: COM9 is used for both telemetry RX and mission TX. `PacketReceiver` owns the `SerialPort` exclusively. `SendRaw()` writes to `_port` directly. The `ProcessBuffer()` framing distinguishes telemetry (164 bytes, sync `0xAA 0x55 0xDD`) from mission responses (36 bytes, sync `0xAA 0x55 0x55 0xBB`).

- **Progress feedback visibility**: Status bar text was too small for the user to monitor upload progress. Resolved with `MissionProgressForm` providing a dedicated modeless window with real-time link status (telemetry byte rate), per-packet log, and final result.

[881] CLAUDE

Now I have the full picture. Here's the answer:

**sgsim receives mission packets whenever it's running** — there's no mode gate on `ReceiveMP_Packets()`. The CMD link thread in `apiocmd.c` reads bytes continuously, detects sync `0xAA 0x55 0x55 0xBB`, sets `MP_Packet=1`, and immediately calls `ReceiveMP_Packets()`. No flight mode check happens here — HEADER_WRITE and all WP_WRITE packets are accepted at any time as long as:

1. **The simulation is running** — the CMD link thread is live and `CmdPortInitialized == 1` (COM24 opened successfully at startup)

2. **`GCS_MCData.Enable_Fixed_Mission == 0`** — this is decoded from the regular GCS command packet (byte 19, bit 6 in `apio_decode.c`). If no GCS is sending that bit high, it defaults to 0. The sgsim screen shows `Enable Fixed Mission = 0` in its status display — confirm this before uploading

3. **Mode is STANDBY or RUNUP for ACTIVATE_MISSION to apply** — the HEADER/WP writes succeed in any mode, but `MCData.ActivateNewMission = 1` (the step that actually arms the new mission) only triggers when mode is STANDBY or RUNUP. If you upload while in AUTO, the packets are received and stored in `MP_WPData[]`, but the mission doesn't activate until you return to STANDBY/RUNUP

**Practical checklist before pressing Send:**
- sgsim is running (not paused/stopped)
- sgsim status shows `Enable Fixed Mission = 0`
- sgsim mode is **STANDBY** (safest) — you should see `MODE=STANDBY` on the sgsim display
- The MissionProgressForm shows `● COM9 LIVE` (telemetry flowing = COM24 link is up)

If the upload completes (all ACKs `0x01 OK`) but the mission doesn't activate in sgsim, check the mode — the FCC was likely in AUTO when ACTIVATE was received.

The sgsim when the app is launched, there is no view of 'Flight Phase' and 'Mode' until I press 'R' (Run). In my view there should be a (load ready) button that sets the required states for upload. [883] CLAUDE

Good design instinct. My take:

**The idea is sound, but scope it carefully.**

The problem you're solving is real — there are at least 3 variables that need to be in the right state simultaneously (`Mode=STANDBY`, `Enable_Fixed_Mission=0`, `CmdPortInitialized=1`), none of which are visible until the sim is running, and none of which have a single obvious UI control. A "Load Ready" button collapses all of that into one action.

**What the button should do on press:**
- Force `MCData.Mode = STANDBY` (or assert a flag the state machine respects on next cycle)
- Force `GCS_MCData.Enable_Fixed_Mission = 0`
- Reset `Header_Written = 0` (clean mission programming state)
- Optionally clear `MP_WPData[]` to avoid stale data

**Enable/disable logic:**
- Disabled until `R` is pressed (CMD port not yet initialized before then)
- Enabled once simulation is running
- Should be a latching toggle — on = "GCS upload armed", off = normal sim operation. Not a momentary button
- On upload complete (ACK_OK on ACTIVATE), auto-release back to off — or at minimum change color

**One risk to flag:** `MCData.Mode` is owned by the autopilot state machine in `Autop.c`. A direct write from the UI thread will work once but the state machine may immediately overwrite it on the next cycle depending on the current flight phase. You need to check whether `Autop.c` transitions *to* STANDBY only on certain conditions, or whether you can hold it there with a flag (`GCS_MCData.GCS_RUNUP_BYPASS_Override` already exists as a precedent for this pattern).

The safer approach: add a `SimData.MissionLoadReady` flag checked at the top of the mode state machine that suppresses transitions away from STANDBY while active.

**Bottom line:** yes, build it — but put it behind the run/stop state and make it a toggle with visible armed/disarmed status, not a fire-and-forget button.

[884] USER
----------------------------------------
When I press the 'R' button, the app state is 'Flight Phase=WAIT' and 'Mode=AUTO'

[885] CLAUDE
----------------------------------------
This is the critical finding. The path to STANDBY is blocked by two things:

**1. `SetMode()` in SGMC.c runs every cycle and locks Mode=AUTO**

The logic is:
- No manual RX (`MC_ManualMode==0`) → falls to `else { MCData.Mode = AUTO; }` every cycle
- There's no `VehicleMode == STANDBY` case — GCS can't command STANDBY through the normal command packet
- Any direct write `MCData.Mode = STANDBY` from a button is immediately overwritten on the next cycle

**2. STANDBY is only reachable from RUNUP in SGFltCtrl.c**

RUNUP → STANDBY requires all sensors valid + `fcc_Time >= 120 seconds` — **or** `bypass == 1`. The `bypass` flag is settable by pressing 'B' on keyboard, or via `GCS_MCData.GCS_RUNUP_BYPASS_Override == 1` after 10 seconds.

**So the "Load Ready" button design must work at the simulation layer, not the autopilot layer:**

The button needs to do **three things atomically**:

```c
// 1. Force into RUNUP (prerequisite for bypass path)
MCData.Mode = RUNUP;

// 2. Suppress SetMode() from overwriting it — add a new flag
SimData.GCSMissionLoadReady = 1;  // new flag

// 3. Trigger bypass → STANDBY on next SGFltCtrl cycle
bypass = 1;
```

And in `SetMode()`, add one guard at the very top:

```c
void SetMode(void) {
    if (SimData.GCSMissionLoadReady == 1)
        return;   // hold — GCS upload in progress
    ...
}
```

Then in `MissionProgramming.c`, after ACTIVATE_MISSION ACK is sent successfully, clear the flag:

```c
SimData.GCSMissionLoadReady = 0;
```

**The "Load Ready" button in sgsim MFC UI:**
- Disabled until 'R' is pressed (`Sys_ON == 1`)
- On press: set `SimData.GCSMissionLoadReady=1`, `MCData.Mode=RUNUP`, `bypass=1`, `Enable_Fixed_Mission=0`, `Header_Written=0`
- Mode will naturally transition RUNUP → STANDBY within 1 cycle via the bypass path
- Auto-clears when ACTIVATE is processed or if button is pressed again (toggle off)

This is the only clean path given the existing state machine architecture.

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- **sgsim architecture**: MFC Windows C++ app; autopilot runs as C code in a thread; MFC source files (MainFrm.cpp, ChildView.cpp, sgsim.cpp) are MISSING — only compiled .obj exist in Debug/; PropertiesWndInteface.cpp IS present and modifiable
- **Mode state machine**: After 'R' pressed, Mode=AUTO/FlightPhase=WAIT. Mode=AUTO is forced by two separate paths: `SetMode()` else clause AND `if (MC_ManualMode==0) MCData.Mode=AUTO` in SGFltCtrl AUTO case. STANDBY only reachable from RUNUP via sensors-valid+120s or bypass=1
- **`bypass` variable**: In SGFltCtrl.c — when set to 1 from RUNUP state, immediately transitions to STANDBY. Set by 'B' keypress or `GCS_MCData.GCS_RUNUP_BYPASS_Override==1 && fcc_Time>10.0`
- **Telemetry**: `SimData.Tel_Ser_Initialized=1` gates `WriteFile()` to `SimData.handleTel` in `Tx_Telemetry()` (apiotel.c). Currently set unconditionally in `Initialize()` in SGMain.cpp
- **Toolbar bitmap constraint**: `IDR_MAINFRAME TOOLBAR 30, 25` uses `res\Toolbar.bmp` with exactly N images for N non-separator buttons. Inserting a button before the last displaces subsequent button images
- **resource.h / sgsim.rc**: Both UTF-16 LE encoded — must use Python `data.decode('utf-16')` / `txt.encode('utf-16')` for editing
- **C89 constraint**: In SGMC.c (C89 mode), `static` declarations must precede all executable statements in a function block
- **.NET Framework 4.8 / C# 7.3**: No switch expressions, no C# 8+ features in GCS project
- **32-byte mission packets**: [0]=VehicleID, [1]=CMD, [2-3]=WPNum, [4-27]=Data, [28-31]=CRC32
- **36-byte FCC response**: [0-3]=0xAA 0x55 0x55 0xBB + [4-31]=28 bytes + [32-35]=CRC32
- **Two mission arrays**: `WPData[]` (active autopilot) vs `MP_WPData[]` (GCS receive buffer); READ commands only work after GCS upload

- **SGMC.c C2143 + C2065 (`prev_Gdc_Mode` undeclared)**: Placed early `return` before `static int prev_Gdc_Mode = MANUAL_EC;` — invalid in C89 which requires all declarations before statements. **Fix**: Moved static declaration to the very top of SetMode() before the guard.

- **RC2104 `ID_GCS_LOAD_READY` undefined**: Python script to update UTF-16 resource.h used wrong line ending pattern (`\n` instead of `\r\n`), silently producing no change. **Fix**: Re-ran Python with `\r\n` in the replacement string; verified with `'GCS_LOAD_READY' in txt2` check.

- **Bad MFC code in PropertiesWndInteface.cpp**: Initially added non-existent macros `BEGIN_MESSAGE_MAP_EXTRA`/`END_MESSAGE_MAP_EXTRA` and a complex CCmdTarget anonymous namespace approach. These don't compile. **Fix**: Removed entirely, replaced with Properties pane approach (adding property to existing CMFCPropertyGridProperty group — the pattern already used throughout the file).

- **'T' terminate button disappeared**: Adding `ID_GCS_LOAD_READY` to the toolbar before `ID_TERMINATE` displaced the Toolbar.bmp image index, stealing TERMINATE's bitmap slot. **Not yet fixed** — fix is to remove `ID_GCS_LOAD_READY` from the toolbar RC (the Properties pane already handles it).

5. Problem Solving:

- **Why Mode=AUTO after 'R'**: Two independent paths force AUTO: `SetMode()` else clause (no VehicleMode for STANDBY) and `if (MC_ManualMode==0) MCData.Mode=AUTO` in SGFltCtrl AUTO case. Both must be guarded by the `GCS_Mission_Load_Ready` flag. The flag directly overrides to STANDBY after both AUTO-forcing paths run.

- **MFC message map unavailable**: Missing MainFrm.cpp/ChildView.cpp means we cannot add ON_COMMAND handlers to the main toolbar command routing chain. Solution: use the Properties pane (`PropertiesWndInteface.cpp` IS present) — same mechanism used for all other sim control toggles (e.g., Enable_Fixed_Mission, DataLogging, etc.).

- **`ActivateNewMission` requirement**: `MCData.ActivateNewMission=1` (set in SGMC.c when Mode==STANDBY/RUNUP) is what gates `ActivateMission()` to actually apply the mission. The flag ensures Mode=STANDBY, which satisfies this condition.

- `Tx_MissProgPacket`'s `#else` branch (sim mode) was empty ("// TBD") → implemented WriteFile

**C. Breakpoint investigation and architecture discovery**:
- `apiocmd.c` is NOT in any VS project — only used in Linux/Code::Blocks build
- The actual command link receive is `ReadCmdLink()` in `hils.cpp`
- **Critical discovery**: `ReadCmdLink` only recognizes sync bytes `0xAA`, `0xA5`, `0x34` for the 4th sync byte — no `0xBB` (mission programming) case
- GCS was sending 32-byte packets with no framing header at all
- Fixed `hils.cpp` to recognize `0xBB` and call `ReceiveMP_Packets(TempBuff)`

**D. Pending**: GCS side must prepend `AA 55 55 BB` before each 32-byte mission packet.

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- **sgsim project structure**: Two VS projects — `sgsim.vcxproj` (MFC app: CHKCHAR.CPP, SGMain.cpp, hils.cpp, PropertiesWndInteface.cpp) and `sgap.vcxproj` (autopilot lib: MissionProgramming.c, SGFltCtrl.c, SGMC.c, apiotel.c, apio_decode.c, etc. → `sgap.lib`)
- **apiocmd.c is Linux-only**: The Windows sim uses `hils.cpp`'s `ReadCmdLink` instead
- **Mission packet framing**: sgsim expects 4-byte sync header `AA 55 55 BB` + 32-byte payload = 36 bytes total for mission programming packets. GCS was sending just 32 bytes (no header)
- **`ReadCmdLink` sync state machine**: Case 0=0xAA, Case 1=0x55, Case 2=0x55, Case 3=4th byte type discriminator. Now includes `0xBB` → `MP_Packet=1`
- **Tel_Ser_Initialized vs Tel_Telemetry_Active**: `Tel_Ser_Initialized` is owned by `InitTelSerialChannel()` in hils.cpp — indicates port is physically open. `Tel_Telemetry_Active` is the new flag that gates periodic telemetry transmission (starts at TO_TAXI).
- **VEHICLE_ID**: `#define VEHICLE_ID (05)` in apconst.h — checked at MissionProgramming.c:189 (`MissProg_DataBuff[0] == VEHICLE_ID`) and apio_decode.c:185. `(02)` was octal = decimal 2, causing all packets to be silently dropped.
- **`ReceiveMP_Packets`**: Declared in `apio.h`, implemented in `MissionProgramming.c`, already included by `hils.cpp` via `#include "autop\apio.h"`
- **sgap.lib**: Static lib built by `sgap.vcxproj`, linked into sgsim. Contains MissionProgramming.obj, SGFltCtrl.obj, SGMC.obj, apiotel.obj, apio_decode.obj, etc.
- **sgsim.rc is UTF-16 LE**: Must use Python `data.decode('utf-16')` / `txt.encode('utf-16')` for editing
- **C89 constraint in SGMC.c**: All declarations before statements in any block
- **GCS_Mission_Load_Ready flag**: Set/cleared by Properties pane; guards SetMode() in SGMC.c; forces STANDBY in SGFltCtrl.c AUTO case; cleared on ACTIVATE_MISSION OK in MissionProgramming.c

  - Added `HexDump` helper method:
  ```csharp
  private static string HexDump(byte[] b)
  {
      if (b == null || b.Length == 0) return "(empty)";
      var sb = new System.Text.StringBuilder(b.Length * 3);
      for (int k = 0; k < b.Length; k++)
      {
          if (k > 0 && k % 16 == 0)
              sb.Append("\r\n         ");
          sb.AppendFormat("{0:X2} ", b[k]);
      }
      return sb.ToString().TrimEnd();
  }
  ```

4. Errors and Fixes:

- **'T' terminate button disappeared**: Inserting `ID_GCS_LOAD_READY` before `ID_TERMINATE` in toolbar stole TERMINATE's bitmap slot. Fixed by removing the button and separator from sgsim.rc via Python (UTF-16 LE).

- **`Tel_Ser_Initialized` misuse**: Set `= 0` in `Initialize()` blocked both telemetry AND mission ACKs. Root cause: the flag is set by `InitTelSerialChannel()` in hils.cpp when the COM port opens successfully. `Initialize()` is called AFTER the port is opened (Properties pane calls `InitTelSerialChannel`, then user presses 'R' which triggers `Initialize()`). Fix: added separate `Tel_Telemetry_Active` flag for the periodic telemetry gate; `Tel_Ser_Initialized` left to hils.cpp ownership exclusively.

- **`Enable_Fixed_Mission` reset**: `Initialize()` unconditionally wrote `GCS_MCData.Enable_Fixed_Mission = 1`, overriding the Properties pane's `= 0` set when GCS Load Ready was armed. Fixed by guarding both `#ifndef RUNSLT` branches with `if (GCS_Mission_Load_Ready == 0)`.

- **`Tx_MissProgPacket` #else branch was empty**: Mission ACKs were never sent in sim mode — the function built `TxBuff` but the Windows path was `// TBD`. Fixed by implementing `WriteFile(SimData.handleTel, TxBuff, 36, ...)` with overlapped I/O.

- **VehicleID mismatch**: `apconst.h` had `#define VEHICLE_ID (02)` (octal 2 = decimal 2 = 0x02) but mission file has `UAV_ID = 5`. MissionProgramming.c line 189 silently drops packets where `MissProg_DataBuff[0] != VEHICLE_ID`. Fixed: changed to `(05)`.

- **apiocmd.c not in VS project**: User couldn't find it. Discovery: apiocmd.c is Linux/Code::Blocks only. Windows sim uses `hils.cpp`'s `ReadCmdLink` for command link receive. Redirected breakpoint advice to `hils.cpp`.

- **hils.cpp ReadCmdLink missing 0xBB handling**: Case 3 didn't accept 0xBB as 4th sync byte, and default case had no `ReceiveMP_Packets` call. GCS was also sending 32-byte packets with no framing at all. Fixed hils.cpp; GCS framing fix is pending.

9. Optional Next Step:

The immediate next step is to add the `AA 55 55 BB` framing on the GCS side. The last assistant message stated:

> "Two bugs: 1. GCS sends 32 bytes with no framing header — sgsim expects `AA 55 55 <type>` + 32 bytes = 36 bytes total. 2. `hils.cpp` has no `0xBB` case — even if GCS adds the header, sgsim would reset sync on the 4th byte. Fix both sides:"

The sgsim side is now done. The pending GCS fix is to add `SendMissionPacket` to `PacketReceiver.cs`:
```csharp
public void SendMissionPacket(byte[] payload)
{
    byte[] framed = new byte[4 + payload.Length];
    framed[0] = 0xAA; framed[1] = 0x55; framed[2] = 0x55; framed[3] = 0xBB;
    Array.Copy(payload, 0, framed, 4, payload.Length);
    _port.Write(framed, 0, framed.Length);
}
```
And update `MissionUploader.cs` and `MissionDownloader.cs` to call `receiver.SendMissionPacket(pkt)` instead of `receiver.SendRaw(pkt)`.

**B. Debugging BP investigation** (completed): User reported BP on `SendRaw` never hit. Diagnosed that (1) `SendRaw` is no longer called since we switched to `SendMissionPacket`, and (2) all three new BPs hit correctly — 3 retries of packet 0, confirming GCS works but sgsim isn't receiving.

**C. Root cause fix: ReadCmdLink never started** (completed this session): Traced why sgsim doesn't receive mission packets. Found `InitCmdLinkSerialChannel` always fails (garbled port string `"\\.\COM24; // 25"` and/or COM24 already exclusively held by `handleTel`), so `CmdLink_Ser_Initialized` stays 0, and `AfxBeginThread(ReadCmdLink)` is gated on that flag — the thread is **never started**. Fixed by switching ReadCmdLink to use `handleTel` + overlapped I/O, and changing the thread launch condition to `Tel_Ser_Initialized`.

**D. sgap cannot be rebuilt** (in progress at summary time): User stated they don't have the sgap source/project. Two previous-session changes that require sgap rebuild are not yet in effect: `VEHICLE_ID (05)` in `apconst.h` and `Tx_MissProgPacket #else` implementation in `apiotel.c`. Need workarounds in sgsim-only code.

**E. Port name question** (answered): User confirmed `"\\\\.\\COM24"` is correct syntax. The `; // 25` was a C comment accidentally included inside the string literal, making the port name invalid. However, even a correct port name wouldn't work because `handleTel` holds COM24 exclusively.

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- **sgsim project structure**: `sgsim.vcxproj` (MFC: SGMain.cpp, hils.cpp, CHKCHAR.CPP, PropertiesWndInteface.cpp) + `sgap.vcxproj` (autopilot static lib: MissionProgramming.c, SGFltCtrl.c, SGMC.c, apiotel.c, apio_decode.c → `sgap.lib`). User **cannot rebuild sgap.lib**.
- **apiocmd.c is Linux-only**: Windows sim uses `hils.cpp`'s `ReadCmdLink` for command link receive.
- **Mission packet framing**: 4-byte sync `AA 55 55 BB` + 32-byte payload = 36 bytes total. GCS now sends 36 bytes via `SendMissionPacket`.
- **ReadCmdLink sync state machine**: Case 0=`0xAA`, Case 1=`0x55`, Case 2=`0x55`, Case 3=4th byte discriminator. After 4 sync bytes, reads 32-byte payload. `0xBB` → `MP_Packet=1` → default case calls `ReceiveMP_Packets(TempBuff)`.
- **handleTel vs handleCmdLink**: `handleTel` opens COM24 with `GENERIC_READ|GENERIC_WRITE`, `FILE_FLAG_OVERLAPPED`, `nShareMode=0` (exclusive). `handleCmdLink` cannot open the same port. `handleTel` is bidirectional — GCS writes to COM9, sgsim reads from COM24 using `handleTel`.
- **Overlapped I/O**: Since `handleTel` was opened with `FILE_FLAG_OVERLAPPED`, all `ReadFile` calls on it require an `OVERLAPPED` structure. Synchronous ReadFile with NULL would return `ERROR_INVALID_PARAMETER`.
- **VEHICLE_ID mismatch** (unresolved without sgap): Old `sgap.lib` has `VEHICLE_ID = (02)` = decimal 2. GCS sends vehicleId=0x05. `ReceiveMP_Packets` at line 189 checks `MissProg_DataBuff[0] == VEHICLE_ID` → fails → packet silently dropped.
- **Tx_MissProgPacket #else empty** (unresolved without sgap): Old `sgap.lib` `Tx_MissProgPacket` has `// TBD` in Windows sim mode → ACKs never sent even if ReceiveMP_Packets processes the packet.
- **MP_Tx_Flag not mode-specific**: The `MCData.MP_Tx_Flag == 1` check in SGFltCtrl.c is inside `if (GCS_MCData.Enable_Telemetry_link)`, runs regardless of STANDBY/AUTO mode.
- **MCData is struct MCType**: Declared as `struct MCType MCData;` in SGFltCtrl.c. `MP_Tx_Flag` is at `apstruct.h` line 397.
- **MP_Buff is a global**: `unsigned char MP_Buff[30];` declared at MissionProgramming.c line 59 — accessible via `extern "C" { extern unsigned char MP_Buff[]; }` in hils.cpp.

3. Files and Code Sections:

- **`C:\Users\uzama\source\repos\GCS_240626\PacketReceiver.cs`**
  - Added `SendMissionPacket` method after `SendRaw` (lines 57-72):
  ```csharp
  public void SendMissionPacket(byte[] payload)
  {
      if (_port == null || !_port.IsOpen)
          throw new InvalidOperationException("[PacketReceiver] Port not open.");
      byte[] framed = new byte[4 + payload.Length];
      framed[0] = 0xAA; framed[1] = 0x55; framed[2] = 0x55; framed[3] = 0xBB;
      Array.Copy(payload, 0, framed, 4, payload.Length);
      _port.Write(framed, 0, framed.Length);
  }
  ```

4. Errors and Fixes:

- **BP on `SendRaw` never hit**: `SendRaw` was no longer called after we changed `MissionUploader` to use `SendMissionPacket`. User was following old debug advice from previous session context. Fixed by explaining to move BP to `SendMissionPacket._port.Write`.

- **ReadCmdLink thread never starts**: `AfxBeginThread` gated on `CmdLink_Ser_Initialized == 1` which is always 0 because `InitCmdLinkSerialChannel` fails. Fixed: changed launch condition to `Tel_Ser_Initialized == 1` in SGMain.cpp.

- **COM24 exclusively locked**: `handleTel` opens COM24 with `nShareMode=0`. `handleCmdLink` cannot open same port. Fixed: ReadCmdLink now uses `handleTel` directly with overlapped I/O.

- **Garbled port name**: `"\\\\.\\COM24; // 25"` — comment accidentally inside string literal. The actual port name string is `\\.\COM24; // 25` which is invalid. This was root cause of `handleCmdLink` always failing. Fixed indirectly by abandoning `handleCmdLink` entirely.

- **if(1) logic error**: Initial refactoring used `if(1)` placeholder which would enter the switch even on read error. Fixed by adding `j = 0; continue;` in error path, which skips the switch by jumping to top of do-while loop.

- **OVERLAPPED mismatch**: `handleTel` opened with `FILE_FLAG_OVERLAPPED`; passing NULL to ReadFile would fail with `ERROR_INVALID_PARAMETER`. Fixed by adding `OVERLAPPED osRead` and using it in all ReadFile calls on `handleTel`.

5. Problem Solving:

**Solved this session:**
- GCS framing: `SendMissionPacket` prepends `AA 55 55 BB`, MissionUploader and MissionDownloader updated
- ReadCmdLink threading: thread now starts when `Tel_Ser_Initialized == 1`
- ReadCmdLink I/O: all reads now use `handleTel` with proper overlapped I/O
- Port string question answered: `"\\\\.\\COM24"` is correct

**Ongoing — requires sgap rebuild OR workaround (user cannot rebuild sgap):**
1. **VEHICLE_ID mismatch**: Old `sgap.lib` has `VEHICLE_ID = (02)` = 0x02. GCS sends vehicleId=0x05. `ReceiveMP_Packets` silently drops all packets. 
   - Cannot fix by changing `TempBuff[0]` before the call (would break CRC which covers byte 0)
   - **Clean fix**: Change GCS vehicleId parameter from 5 to 2 in Form1.cs `OnMissionSendRequested`
2. **Tx_MissProgPacket no-op**: Old `sgap.lib` `#else` branch is `// TBD`. Even if ReceiveMP_Packets processes a packet and sets `MCData.MP_Tx_Flag = 1`, the ACK is never sent.
   - **Workaround**: In hils.cpp ReadCmdLink, after `ReceiveMP_Packets(TempBuff)`, add `extern "C"` declarations for `MCData` (struct MCType) and `MP_Buff` (unsigned char[]), then directly build and write the 36-byte ACK frame via `WriteFile(SimData.handleTel, ...)` if `MCData.MP_Tx_Flag == 1`.

- **Workaround for Tx_MissProgPacket no-op (cannot rebuild sgap)**: In hils.cpp ReadCmdLink `MP_Packet == 1` branch, after `ReceiveMP_Packets(TempBuff)`, add extern declarations and directly send 36-byte ACK via `handleTel`:
  ```c
  extern "C" { extern struct MCType MCData; extern unsigned char MP_Buff[]; }
  // After ReceiveMP_Packets:
  if (MCData.MP_Tx_Flag == 1)
  {
      static OVERLAPPED osACKWrite;
      static int osACKWriteInit = 0;
      unsigned char ACK_Frame[36];
      unsigned long ackCRC;
      DWORD nACKWritten;
      MCData.MP_Tx_Flag = 0;
      ACK_Frame[0]=0xAA; ACK_Frame[1]=0x55; ACK_Frame[2]=0x55; ACK_Frame[3]=0xBB;
      memcpy(&ACK_Frame[4], MP_Buff, 28);
      ackCRC = CalcCRC32(&ACK_Frame[4], 0, 28);
      ACK_Frame[32]=(unsigned char)(ackCRC&0xFF);
      ACK_Frame[33]=(unsigned char)((ackCRC>>8)&0xFF);
      ACK_Frame[34]=(unsigned char)((ackCRC>>16)&0xFF);
      ACK_Frame[35]=(unsigned char)((ackCRC>>24)&0xFF);
      if (!osACKWriteInit) { memset(&osACKWrite,0,sizeof(osACKWrite)); osACKWriteInit=1; }
      WriteFile(SimData.handleTel, ACK_Frame, 36, NULL, &osACKWrite);
      if (GetLastError()==ERROR_IO_PENDING)
          GetOverlappedResult(SimData.handleTel, &osACKWrite, &nACKWritten, FALSE);
  }
  ```
- **Rebuild sgsim only** (not sgap): hils.cpp and SGMain.cpp were changed this session; sgsim rebuild required.

All three changes are in place. Here's a summary of what was done and why:

**Form1.cs** — `OnMissionSendRequested` now forces `vehicleId = 2` before the upload. The mission file stores UAV_ID=5, but the old `sgap.lib` was compiled with `VEHICLE_ID=(02)` (octal 2 = decimal 2). `ReceiveMP_Packets` checks `MissProg_DataBuff[0] == VEHICLE_ID` on the very first byte of every packet, so a mismatch silently drops everything.

This bypasses the empty `Tx_MissProgPacket` `#else` stub.

The root cause: `InitTelSerialChannel` is called once at startup (default "No HILS" sets `handleTel`, `Tel_Ser_Initialized=1`). The logic is self-consistent:

- When `InitTelSerialChannel` runs on first open (from "No HILS" default), `HILSgcsONLY == 0` → STANDBY not forced. Mode is left at whatever the simulator started with.
- When the user later switches to **"HILS with GCS ONLY"**, `HILSgcsONLY` is set to 1 first, then `InitTelSerialChannel` is called again — the idempotency guard fires, confirms `Tel_Ser_Initialized = 1`, and now `HILSgcsONLY == 1` → `MCData.Mode = STANDBY`.

Once in the STANDBY case in SGFltCtrl, `SetMode()` is only called when `MissionProgrammed == 1`. While uploading (`MissionProgrammed == 0`), Mode stays STANDBY, so `SGMC.c` sets `ActivateNewMission = 1`, and `ActivateMission()` accepts the packet instead of returning MISSION_PROG_DENIED. After ACTIVATE_MISSION succeeds, `MissionProgrammed` becomes 1, `SetMode()` runs, and the AP transitions naturally to AUTO.

Rebuild sgsim, then in the Properties panel set **Real time → Yes**, **HILS Option → "HILS with GCS ONLY"** — the output window should confirm "MCData.Mode forced to STANDBY" before you run the upload.

That sets `GCS_Mission_Load_Ready = 1`, which flips `Enable_Fixed_Mission` to 0, which lets SGMC.c reach the `ActivateNewMission = 1` branch (Mode=RUNUP satisfies it), and `ActivateMission()` will accept the packet.

So the correct sequence in sgsim before uploading from GCS:
1. Properties: **HILS Option → "HILS with GCS ONLY"**, **Real time → Yes**
2. Press **'L'** (or the toolbar GCS_LOAD_READY button) — you should see "GCS_Mission_Load_Ready = 1" in the log

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- **Virtual COM port pair**: GCS writes to COM9, sgsim reads from COM24 (`handleTel`). GCS reads on COM9, sgsim writes to COM24. Confirmed correct wire data `AA 55 55 BB 02 51...` via serial terminal on COM24.
- **`handleTel` exclusivity**: Opened with `nShareMode=0` (exclusive). `InitCmdLinkSerialChannel` cannot open COM24 because `handleTel` already holds it. ReadCmdLink was changed (previous session) to use `handleTel` with overlapped I/O.
- **`STANDBY = 3`** (apconst.h line 69). Mode=RUNUP (value not STANDBY) is also sufficient: SGMC.c line 3817 includes both: `if(MCData.Mode == STANDBY || MCData.Mode == RUNUP || ...)`.
- **`Enable_Fixed_Mission` gate**: SGMC.c takes either the `PrepareFixedMission` branch (when `Enable_Fixed_Mission==1`) or the `ActivateNewMission` branch. Only the latter sets `MCData.ActivateNewMission=1`, which allows `ActivateMission()` to succeed.
- **`InitConditions=0` hardcoded**: `switch(InitConditions) case 0: // Taxi` in SGMain.cpp runs at initialization with `GCS_Mission_Load_Ready=0` → `Enable_Fixed_Mission=1` → `PrepareFixedMission()` → `MCData.MissionProgrammed=1` before user can arm GCS_LOAD_READY.
- **Race condition candidate**: SGFltCtrl.c lines 593-597 run every simulation cycle: `if (MCData.MP_Tx_Flag == 1) { MCData.MP_Tx_Flag = 0; Tx_MissProgPacket(MP_Buff); }`. This clears `MP_Tx_Flag` before ReadCmdLink can check it — a potential race between the simulation thread and ReadCmdLink thread.
- **`ReceiveMP_Packets` CRC check**: `CalcCRC32(DataBuff, 0, 28)` compared against `DataBuff[28..31]`. If CRC fails, `Decode_MissProgPacket` is never called and `MP_Tx_Flag` stays 0. CRC mismatch between GCS `MissionFile.Crc32` and sgsim `CalcCRC32` would cause silent drop.
- **`MP_Tx_Flag` flow**: `PrepareAck()` in MissionProgramming.c fills `MP_Buff[0..4]` and sets `MCData.MP_Tx_Flag=1`. ReadCmdLink's workaround checks this flag after `ReceiveMP_Packets` and sends a 36-byte framed ACK directly via `WriteFile(handleTel, ...)`.
- **Overlapped I/O requirement**: `handleTel` opened with `FILE_FLAG_OVERLAPPED`. All `ReadFile`/`WriteFile` calls on it require an `OVERLAPPED` struct.
- **`VEHICLE_ID=(02)`**: old sgap.lib compiled with octal 02 = decimal 2. GCS vehicleId overridden to 2 in Form1.cs.

4. Errors and Fixes:

- **TX log showed only 32 bytes without sync header**: `SendMissionPacket` builds its own internal `framed` byte array and never modifies `pkt`. Fixed by building `wire[]` in the log statement.
- **`Tel_Ser_Initialized` set to 0 on second `InitTelSerialChannel` call**: When user switches to "HILS with GCS ONLY", `InitTelSerialChannel` is called again; `CreateFileA` fails (COM24 already open), `HandleFlag=0`, `Tel_Ser_Initialized=0`. Thread-start condition fails. Fixed: idempotency guard at top of `InitTelSerialChannel`.
- **No STANDBY in HILS GCS Only**: RUNUP→STANDBY requires IMU, GPS, ECU, RA, ServoFB, DGPS_DIFF, 120s — none available in simulation. Fixed: force `MCData.Mode=STANDBY` in `InitTelSerialChannel` when `HILSgcsONLY==1`. Note: RUNUP is also acceptable since SGMC.c accepts both.
- **Pre-programmed mission starts on 'R'**: `InitConditions=0` case 0 at startup sets `Enable_Fixed_Mission=1` → `MissionProgrammed=1` before user arms GCS_LOAD_READY. Then STANDBY case: `MissionProgrammed==1` → `SetMode()` → AUTO. Fixed: ARMED handler in PropertiesWndInteface.cpp now resets `MCData.MissionProgrammed=0` and `MCData.Mode=STANDBY`.
- **BP 5 (`if (MCData.MP_Tx_Flag == 1)`) hit but flag is 0**: Currently unresolved. `ReceiveMP_Packets` was called but returned without setting `MP_Tx_Flag`. Two possible causes: (a) CRC failure in `ReceiveMP_Packets` — `Decode_MissProgPacket` never called, (b) race condition: `SGFltCtrl` (main simulation thread) cleared `MP_Tx_Flag=0` between `PrepareAck` setting it and ReadCmdLink checking it.

**Solved:**
- GCS TX log now shows correct 36-byte wire frame
- `InitTelSerialChannel` idempotency prevents `Tel_Ser_Initialized` being incorrectly cleared
- ReadCmdLink thread starts correctly in HILS-GCS-ONLY mode
- Thread reads from `handleTel` using proper overlapped I/O
- `MCData.Mode=STANDBY` forced when arming GCS_LOAD_READY (with `MissionProgrammed=0` reset)
- Thread IS running and receiving packets (BP 1 + BP 5 hit confirmed)

- `MCData.MP_Tx_Flag` is 0 at BP 5, meaning `PrepareAck` either was not called (CRC failure most likely) or its result was cleared by the SGFltCtrl race condition. The upload still fails — no ACK is sent back to GCS.

7. Pending Tasks:

- **Diagnose why `MP_Tx_Flag` is 0** at BP 5: Either CRC mismatch between GCS `MissionFile.Crc32` and sgsim `CalcCRC32`, or race condition where SGFltCtrl clears the flag before ReadCmdLink checks it.
- **If CRC mismatch**: verify GCS CRC implementation vs sgsim's `CalcCRC32`. The GCS uses `MissionFile.Crc32(pkt, 0, 28)` and sgsim uses `CalcCRC32(DataBuff, 0, 28)`.
- **If race condition**: The SGFltCtrl runs in the main thread every cycle, clears `MP_Tx_Flag=0` via `Tx_MissProgPacket` call. ReadCmdLink is a separate thread. `MP_Tx_Flag` could be cleared between `PrepareAck` and ReadCmdLink's check. Fix: ReadCmdLink should build the ACK from `MP_Buff` directly without relying on `MP_Tx_Flag`.

8. Current Work:

Immediately before the summary request, the user reported: **"it reached BP 5 'if (MCData.MP_Tx_Flag == 1)' but the condition did not converge to 1"**

This confirms:
- ReadCmdLink thread IS running ✓
- 4 sync bytes `AA 55 55 BB` were received ✓
- 32-byte payload was read ✓
- `ReceiveMP_Packets(TempBuff)` was called ✓
- Code reached `if (MCData.MP_Tx_Flag == 1)` but flag = 0 ✗

The most likely explanation is a **CRC failure** in `ReceiveMP_Packets`. The function at line 145 of MissionProgramming.c computes `CalcCRC32(DataBuff, 0, 28)` and compares to `DataBuff[28..31]`. If the CRC bytes don't match, it increments `GCS_MissProgData.CRCFailCounter`, sets `GCS_MissProgData.CRCFailFlag=1`, and returns without calling `Decode_MissProgPacket()` or `PrepareAck()`, leaving `MP_Tx_Flag=0`.

A secondary possibility is a **race condition**: SGFltCtrl.c lines 593-597 run in the main simulation thread every cycle: `if (MCData.MP_Tx_Flag == 1) { MCData.MP_Tx_Flag = 0; Tx_MissProgPacket(MP_Buff); }`. If `PrepareAck` set `MP_Tx_Flag=1` and then SGFltCtrl ran before ReadCmdLink checked it, the flag would be cleared to 0 (with the empty `Tx_MissProgPacket` doing nothing).

9. Optional Next Step:

Based on BP 5 being hit with `MP_Tx_Flag == 0`, the next step is to determine **why `PrepareAck` wasn't called** (or was cleared). The most productive approach is to check whether the CRC is failing in `ReceiveMP_Packets`:

Add a BP at **MissionProgramming.c line 161** (`Decode_MissProgPacket()` call inside the CRC-pass branch) and at **line 180** (`GCS_MissProgData.CRCFailCounter++` in the CRC-fail branch). If BP at line 180 hits and line 161 does not, CRC is failing and the GCS CRC implementation (`MissionFile.Crc32`) needs to be compared byte-for-byte against sgsim's `CalcCRC32`.

If line 161 hits but `MP_Tx_Flag` is still 0 at BP 5, then the race condition is the culprit — SGFltCtrl cleared the flag. The fix in that case: in ReadCmdLink's MP_Packet branch, instead of checking `MP_Tx_Flag`, directly check `GCS_MissProgData.FeshDataFrame` (set to 1 on CRC pass) and build the ACK from `MP_Buff` immediately after `ReceiveMP_Packets` returns, without waiting for the flag.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:

Continuing from a previous session to make GCS mission upload work end-to-end between `GCS_240626` (C# WinForms GCS) and `sgsim` (MFC C++ simulator). The current goal is to achieve a complete, successful mission upload including the ACTIVATE_MISSION step.

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- **Virtual COM port pair**: GCS writes to COM9, sgsim reads from COM24 (`handleTel`). GCS reads from COM9, sgsim writes to COM24. Standard null-modem virtual pair.
- **`handleTel` exclusivity**: Opened with `nShareMode=0` (exclusive). ReadCmdLink uses it via overlapped I/O.
- **CRC algorithms**: Two different CRC-32 variants in play:
  - `MissionFile.Crc32` (standard ISO CRC-32): seed=`0xFFFFFFFF`, final XOR `0xFFFFFFFF`
  - `CalcCRC32` in sgap/apio.c: seed=`0x00000000`, no final XOR, polynomial reflected `0xEDB88320`
  - `Calculate_CRC32` in MissionProgramming.c: running accumulator into global `MP_CRC`, same table/polynomial as CalcCRC32, seed=0 per mission
- **`VEHICLE_ID = (02)`**: Octal literal `02` = decimal 2. Compiled into sgap.lib. GCS must send vehicleId=2.
- **`PrepareAck` behavior**: Fills `MP_Buff[0..4]` only (vehicleId, CMD, WP#lo, WP#hi, ACK code). Sets `MCData.MP_Tx_Flag = 1`. `MP_Buff` is 30 bytes total.
- **`MP_Tx_Flag` race**: `SGFltCtrl.c` runs every simulation cycle in main thread: `if (GCS_MCData.Enable_Telemetry_link) { if (MP_Tx_Flag==1) { MP_Tx_Flag=0; Tx_MissProgPacket(MP_Buff); } }`. Can clear the flag between `ReceiveMP_Packets` returning and ReadCmdLink checking it.
- **Mission CRC (`Calc_MP_CRC`)**: Running CRC (seed=0) over `MP_Header_Buff[4..23]` (20 bytes) + each WP's `MP_Buff[4..27]` (24 bytes) + POI/SEARCH bytes if applicable. Result compared against `MP_Header_Buff[24..27]` = header packet pkt[24..27] = data[20..23]. Currently zeros in GCS → always fails with `MISSION_CRC_FAILED`.
- **`ReceiveMP_Packets` flow**: CRC check → if pass: copies to `MissProg_DataBuff`, sets `FeshDataFrame=1`, calls `Decode_MissProgPacket` → VEHICLE_ID check → switch on CMD → `PrepareAck` → `MP_Tx_Flag=1`.
- **`STANDBY = 3`** (apconst.h). Mode forced to STANDBY in `InitTelSerialChannel` when `HILSgcsONLY==1`.
- **`GCS_Mission_Load_Ready` ARMED handler** resets `MCData.MissionProgrammed=0` and `MCData.Mode=STANDBY`.
- **ReadCmdLink ACK workaround**: Sends 36-byte frame (AA 55 55 BB + MP_Buff[0..27] + CRC) directly via `WriteFile(handleTel, ...)` since `Tx_MissProgPacket` is stubbed `// TBD` in old sgap.lib.
- **ACTIVATE_MISSION**: Checks all WPs received, then calls `Calc_MP_CRC()` which does the running CRC check. Only calls `ActivateMission()` if CRC matches.

3. Files and Code Sections:

- **`C:\Users\uzama\source\repos\GCS_240626\MissionPacketEncoder.cs`**
  - Critical file: encodes all mission packets; `AppendCRC` was using wrong CRC seed
  - Fixed `AppendCRC` to use new private `CalcCRC32(seed=0)` instead of `MissionFile.Crc32`
  - `PACKET_SIZE=32`, `DATA_OFFSET=4`, `DATA_LEN=24`, `CRC_OFFSET=28`
  - Current state of AppendCRC and CalcCRC32:
  ```csharp
  private static void AppendCRC(byte[] pkt)
  {
      uint crc = CalcCRC32(pkt, 0, CRC_OFFSET);
      pkt[28] = (byte)(crc & 0xFF);
      pkt[29] = (byte)((crc >> 8) & 0xFF);
      pkt[30] = (byte)((crc >> 16) & 0xFF);
      pkt[31] = (byte)((crc >> 24) & 0xFF);
  }
  private static uint CalcCRC32(byte[] data, int start, int end)
  {
      uint crc = 0u;
      for (int i = start; i < end; i++)
      {
          crc ^= data[i];
          for (int k = 0; k < 8; k++)
              crc = (crc & 1u) != 0u ? (0xEDB88320u ^ (crc >> 1)) : (crc >> 1);
      }
      return crc;
  }
  ```
  - **PENDING**: `Encode()` must be modified to compute running mission CRC and store it in header `data[20..23]` (= pkt[24..27]).
  - `BuildHeaderPacket` layout: pkt[0]=vehicleId, pkt[1]=CMD_HEADER_WRITE(0x51), pkt[2-3]=WP#0, pkt[4-11]=timestamp, pkt[12]=UAVid, pkt[13-21]=name, pkt[22-23]=TotalWP, **pkt[24-27]=file CRC (currently zeros)**, pkt[28-31]=per-packet CRC

  private static uint CalcCRC32(byte[] data, int start, int end)
  {
      uint crc = 0u;

          crc ^= data[i];
          for (int k = 0; k < 8; k++)

8. Current Work:

Immediately before the summary request, the assistant had identified that `Calc_MP_CRC` in `MissionProgramming.c` (line 688-756) compares a running CRC of all mission data against `MP_Header_Buff[24..27]`, which corresponds to header packet `data[20..23]`. The GCS `BuildHeaderPacket` leaves `data[20..23]` = zeros, guaranteeing `MISSION_CRC_FAILED` on every ACTIVATE_MISSION. The assistant had just finished reading `MissionPacketEncoder.Encode()` (lines 89-120) to prepare for editing it to add the mission CRC computation.

The `Calculate_CRC32` algorithm (line 800-808):
```c
void Calculate_CRC32(unsigned char *pkt, int start, int end)
{
    int i;
    for (i = start; i < end; i++)
    {
        CRC_Byte_Count++;
        MP_CRC = (MP_CRC >> 8) ^ Table[pkt[i] ^ MP_CRC & 0xff];
    }
}
```
- Identical to CalcCRC32 but accumulates into global `MP_CRC` (initialized to 0 in Calc_MP_CRC)
- Coverage: `header[4..23]` (20 bytes) + `WP[4..27]` (24 bytes) + `POI[4..27]` + `SEARCH[4..27]` per WP, in upload order

The planned fix for `Encode()` in `MissionPacketEncoder.cs`:
1. Build header packet first (data[20..23] = zeros)
2. Build all WP/POI/SEARCH packets (same order as Calc_MP_CRC processes: WP0, POI0?, SEARCH0?, WP1, ...)
3. Compute running CRC: `CalcCRC32(headerPkt, 4, 24, init=0)` then for each WP packet `CalcCRC32(pkt, 4, 28, running_crc)`
4. Store mission CRC into `headerPkt[24..27]`
5. Recompute `headerPkt[28..31]` via `AppendCRC(headerPkt)` (per-packet CRC covers [0..27] including now-set [24..27])

The `CalcCRC32` method needs an overload accepting an initial value so the running CRC can be accumulated across multiple packet ranges:
```csharp
private static uint CalcCRC32(byte[] data, int start, int end, uint init = 0u)
{
    uint crc = init;
    for (int i = start; i < end; i++)
    {
        crc ^= data[i];
        for (int k = 0; k < 8; k++)
            crc = (crc & 1u) != 0u ? (0xEDB88320u ^ (crc >> 1)) : (crc >> 1);
    }
    return crc;
}
```
